13	  dispatch (`loop_spacing`/`loop_byte`/`loop_comment` + the halting classes
14	  `loop_trailing/split/unknown_high/unknown_low/short`).
15	  `#print axioms Hex0.Refine.core_refines` → `[propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound]`
16	  (no `sorryAx`). `grep -c '  sorry' lean/Hex0/Refine.lean` → 0.
17	- **BUILD GOTCHA (cost real time):** `lake build`'s default target only built
18	  what `lean/Hex0.lean` imports. That root did NOT import `Refine`, so
19	  `lake build` reported success *without ever type-checking `Refine.lean`* (and
20	  served a stale `.olean`). Fixed: `Hex0.lean` now imports `Refine`/`Image`/
21	  `Harness`/`Certify`. **To validate `Refine` directly without cache, use
22	  `lake env lean Hex0/Refine.lean`** (errors print top-down; exit 0 = clean).
23	  Also note `set`/`List.getD_eq_getElem` are Mathlib/Batteries-only — unavailable
24	  here; use `let x := e; have h : x = e := rfl; rw [← h] at <hyp>` and
25	  `(List.getElem_eq_getD 0)` instead.
26	- The remaining frontier is now **task #7** (ISA cross-check) and the single
27	  Coq `Refine.v` hole `loop_iteration` (the per-token dispatch; `core_refines`
28	  itself is proved modulo it).
29	
30	## Environment gotchas (these cost real time — don't rediscover)
31	
32	- **Lean is 4.30.0 via elan; there is NO Mathlib.** Consequences:
33	  - **Banned tactics/lemmas**: `norm_num`, `ring`/`ring_nf`, `set ... with`,
34	    `omega` does NOT evaluate `2^64` reliably as a bound unless the other facts
35	    pin it (it's usually fine, but for `a < 2^64` from `a < small` it works).
36	    `le_refl` unqualified is absent → use `Nat.le_refl`.
37	  - **Use instead**: `decide` (for closed nat/BitVec goals incl. `2 < 2^64`),
38	    `omega` (linear nat), `simp`, `Nat.le_refl`, `List.ext_getElem`.
39	  - `set x := e with h` → replace with `let x := e` + `have h : x = e := rfl` +
40	    `rw [← h] at <hyps mentioning e>`.
41	- **`set_option maxRecDepth 4000 in` MUST come BEFORE the doc comment**, not
42	  between the doc comment and the `theorem`. `/-- … -/ set_option … in theorem`
43	  is a parse error ("unexpected token set_option").
44	- **`decide` chokes on free variables.** `(by decide)` proving e.g.
45	  `BitVec.ofNat 64 (coreAddr + off) ≠ 0` fails when `off` is symbolic. Use
46	  `ofNat_ne` (proved) with explicit bound proofs, or reduce to a closed term
47	  first (`simp only [Image.coreAddr]; omega`).
48	- `decide` needs `maxRecDepth ~4000` whenever it evaluates `Image.coreBytes.length`
49	  (a 324-element list) or 64-bit BitVec arithmetic with ~2³¹ addresses.
50	- **`by` inside an anonymous constructor `⟨…⟩` is greedy** — it swallows the
51	  following tuple elements. Always parenthesize: `⟨(by decide), …⟩`.
52	- `simp` will collapse `x = x` to `True`; then provide `trivial`, not `rfl`.
53	- **`native_decide` works but adds the Lean compiler to the TCB** — used only in

60	  for spec stuff (`Hex0.decodeS`, `Hex0.nibble`, `Hex0.coreS

5	
6	## Proven (NOT in the TCB)
7	
8	- **The `decode` spec** (`coq/Spec.v`, `lean/Hex0/Spec.lean`) — the meaning of
9	  hex0. The two definitions compute identically on a battery of inputs, and the
10	  Lean `decodeS` is **proved equivalent to the published BNF grammar of HEX0.md**
11	  (`lean/Hex0/Grammar.lean`): `decodeS .High inp = (out,st) ↔ Parse inp out st`,
12	  with the grammar shown total (`parse_total`) and deterministic (`parse_det`) —
13	  every input is *either* a valid program (→ `Ok`) *or* exactly one error class,
14	  and the classification matches the spec.
15	- **The RV64I model** (`*/Rv64i.*`) executes the *actual* `core` bytes and
16	  matches `coreSpec` (differential battery + the embedded input).
17	- **Concrete certification** (`*/Certify.*`) — the deployed bytes equal

21	  proved, `sorry`-free** (axioms: `propext`/`Classical.choice`/`Quot.sound`).
22	  The **Coq `Refine.v`** port now proves `core_refines` modulo the single

24	  core_refines` ⇒ `loop_iteration` + `functional_extensionality_dep`, a standard
25	  consistent axiom for `mem : Z → Z` state equality). Everything assembling the

44	   - streams `out_len` output bytes and signals completion.

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  22:00:43; tool 9ms

```
1	# Proof outline — verified hex0 (the refinement methodology)
2	
3	This documents *how* the hex0 verification is structured, so the proof can be
4	audited, maintained, and **re-implemented in another proof assistant** (the Coq
5	port follows this outline verbatim). Read with `STATUS.md` (state), `TCB.md`
6	(trust boundary), `HEX0.md` (the language).
7	
8	## 1. The verification tower
9	
10	```
11	   HEX0.md BNF  ⟺  decodeS / coreSpec  ⟸  RV64I model running the real bytes
12	   (grammar)        (functional spec)       (binary, byte-for-byte)
13	   └─ Grammar.lean ─┘└──────────── Refine.lean (core_refines) ───────────┘
14	```
15	
16	Two independent proofs meet at the functional spec:
17	
18	- **`Grammar.lean`** — the published BNF (`HEX0.md`) `⟺` the spec `decodeS`
19	  (sound + complete; the grammar is total and deterministic). Anchors "is the
20	  spec the language we documented?".
21	- **`Refine.lean`** — `core_refines`: for **all** inputs, the real `core` bytes
22	  executed on the RV64I model compute exactly `coreSpec`. Anchors "do the bytes
23	  that run implement the spec?".
24	
25	Everything below is the structure of `Refine.lean` (the hard half), then the
26	`Grammar.lean` layer, then the Coq port plan.
27	
28	## 2. Objects
29	
30	- **Model** (`Rv64i`): `State = (reg, pc, mem)`, a pure `step : State → State`
31	  over the 12 instruction forms `core` uses (`addi add or slli lbu sb beq blt
32	  bge bgeu jal jalr`), `runFuel`/`runUntil` to iterate. No CSRs, traps,
33	  privilege, or stack (`core` is a leaf function — see TCB / the input contract).
34	- **Spec** (`Spec`): `decodeS : St → List Nat → (List Nat × Status)`, a two-state
35	  (`High`/`Low`) functional decoder; `coreSpec` wraps it with the output-capacity
36	  (`OutputShort`) bound.
37	- **Harness**: `initOn`/`mkInit` (the entry state: code+input loaded, `a0..a3`
38	  set, `ra=0`), `observe`/`runOn` (run and read back `a0`,`a1`, output region).
39	
40	## 3. The theorem and its preconditions
41	
42	```
43	core_refines : ∀ inp cap, WellFormed inp cap →
44	                 ∃ fuel, observe inp cap fuel = coreSpec inp cap
45	```
46	`WellFormed inp cap` (the input contract):
47	- `in_fits  : inputAddr + |inp| ≤ outAddr`   — input/output regions disjoint.
48	- `out_fits : outAddr + cap < 2^64`           — output region fits, no wraparound.
49	- `bytes_ok : ∀ b ∈ inp, b < 256`             — inputs are bytes.
50	
51	Implicit (in `initOn`): fixed memory layout (code abuts input: `coreAddr+324 =
52	inputAddr`), `ra=0` with "return = halt (pc→0)", no stack used. (See TCB.)
53	
54	## 4. Methodology — refinement by loop invariant + induction (4 steps)
55	
56	1. **Base case** (`core_eof`): from the loop head with input exhausted, the
57	   machine runs `bgeu(taken);li a0,0;mv a1,t1;ret`, halting `Ok` with output
58	   preserved.
59	2. **Loop-state model** (`LoopInv inp cap s rest emitted`): a 16-field invariant
60	   relating a mid-execution state to a *partial* run of `decodeS` — `rest` is the
61	   unconsumed input suffix, `emitted` the bytes written, with the telescoping
62	   field `spec_link : decodeS High inp = (emitted ++ (decodeS High rest).1, …)`,
63	   plus register/memory facts and the static region bounds (`in_fits`,`out_lt`).
64	3. **Token decomposition**:
65	   - *spec side* (`decodeS_spacing/byte/comment_skip`): one `decodeS` step per
66	     token class.
67	   - *machine side* (`loop_iteration`): from a non-empty `rest`, the machine
68	     either returns to the loop head with a strictly shorter `rest` and `LoopInv`
69	     preserved, or halts in a `coreSpec`-correct error state. A **dispatch on the
70	     head char's class** (see §6).
71	4. **Induction** (`loop_correct`): structural induction on a fuel bound on
72	   `|rest|`; base = `core_eof`, step = `loop_iteration`, chained by `runFuel_add`,
73	   telescoped by `spec_link`. Then assemble with the **prologue**
74	   (`init_loopinv`) and the **`observe↔coreSpec` conversion**.
75	
76	## 5. The lemma DAG (depe
… [truncated 6272 chars]
```

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  22:00:54; tool 7ms

```
1	/-
2	  A minimal, executable RV64I model -- exactly the 12 instruction encodings
3	  used by `bare/core.s`:
4	
5	    ADDI ADD OR SLLI LBU SB BEQ BLT BGE BGEU JAL JALR
6	
7	  (li, mv collapse to ADDI; j = JAL x0; ret = JALR x0,ra,0). No LUI/AUIPC, no
8	  other loads/stores -- this is the whole trusted ISA surface for the hex0 rung.
9	
10	  Words/addresses are `BitVec 64`, memory is byte-addressed (`BitVec 64 -> BitVec 8`),
11	  instructions are decoded from little-endian 32-bit words. The model is
12	  executable (`#eval`) so it can be run on the actual binary's bytes and checked
13	  against the QEMU run before any proof (see Hex0/Validate.lean).
14	-/
15	
16	namespace Rv64i
17	
18	abbrev Word := BitVec 64
19	abbrev Byte := BitVec 8
20	
21	structure State where
22	  reg : Nat → Word          -- x0..x31; x0 hardwired to 0 by rget/rset
23	  pc  : Word
24	  mem : Word → Byte
25	
26	/-- Read register `i` (x0 reads as 0). -/
27	@[inline] def State.rget (s : State) (i : Nat) : Word :=
28	  if i = 0 then 0 else s.reg i
29	
30	/-- Write register `i` (writes to x0 are ignored). -/
31	@[inline] def State.rset (s : State) (i : Nat) (v : Word) : State :=
32	  if i = 0 then s else { s with reg := fun j => if j = i then v else s.reg j }
33	
34	@[inline] def State.setPc (s : State) (p : Word) : State := { s with pc := p }
35	
36	@[inline] def State.loadByte (s : State) (a : Word) : Byte := s.mem a
37	
38	@[inline] def State.storeByte (s : State) (a : Word) (b : Byte) : State :=
39	  { s with mem := fun x => if x = a then b else s.mem x }
40	
41	/-- Fetch the little-endian 32-bit word at `pc`. -/
42	def fetch32 (s : State) : BitVec 32 :=
43	  let b0 := (s.mem s.pc).setWidth 32
44	  let b1 := (s.mem (s.pc + 1)).setWidth 32
45	  let b2 := (s.mem (s.pc + 2)).setWidth 32
46	  let b3 := (s.mem (s.pc + 3)).setWidth 32
47	  b0 ||| (b1 <<< 8) ||| (b2 <<< 16) ||| (b3 <<< 24)
48	
49	/-- Extract `len` bits starting at bit `lo` as a Nat. -/
50	@[inline] def field (w : BitVec 32) (lo len : Nat) : Nat :=
51	  (w.toNat >>> lo) &&& (2 ^ len - 1)
52	
53	inductive Instr where
54	  | addi (rd rs1 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 12)
55	  | add  (rd rs1 rs2 : Nat)
56	  | or   (rd rs1 rs2 : Nat)
57	  | slli (rd rs1 : Nat) (shamt : Nat)
58	  | lbu  (rd rs1 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 12)
59	  | sb   (rs1 rs2 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 12)
60	  | beq  (rs1 rs2 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 13)
61	  | blt  (rs1 rs2 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 13)
62	  | bge  (rs1 rs2 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 13)
63	  | bgeu (rs1 rs2 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 13)
64	  | jal  (rd : Nat) (imm : BitVec 21)
65	  | jalr (rd rs1 : Nat) (imm : BitVec 12)
66	  | unknown
67	deriving Repr, DecidableEq
68	
69	def decode (w : BitVec 32) : Instr :=
70	  let opcode := field w 0 7
71	  let rd     := field w 7 5
72	  let funct3 := field w 12 3
73	  let rs1    := field w 15 5
74	  let rs2    := field w 20 5
75	  let funct7 := field w 25 7
76	  let immI   : BitVec 12 := BitVec.ofNat 12 (field w 20 12)
77	  let shamt  := field w 20 6
78	  -- S-type immediate: [11:5]=funct7, [4:0]=rd
79	  let immS   : BitVec 12 := BitVec.ofNat 12 ((funct7 <<< 5) ||| rd)
80	  -- B-type immediate: [12]=b31 [11]=b7 [10:5]=b[30:25] [4:1]=b[11:8] [0]=0
81	  let immB   : BitVec 13 := BitVec.ofNat 13
82	      (((field w 31 1) <<< 12) ||| ((field w 7 1) <<< 11) |||
83	       ((field w 25 6) <<< 5)  ||| ((field w 8 4) <<< 1))
84	  -- J-type immediate: [20]=b31 [19:12]=b[19:12] [11]=b20 [10:1]=b[30:21] [0]=0
85	  let immJ   : BitVec 21 := BitVec.ofNat 21
86	      (((field w 31 1) <<< 20) ||| ((field w 12 8) <<< 12) |||
87	       ((field w 20 1) <<< 11) ||| ((field w 21 10) <<< 1))
88	  match opcode with
89	  | 0x13 => -- OP-IMM
90	      match funct3 with
91	      | 0x0 => .addi rd rs1 immI
92	      | 0x1 => if funct7 = 0 then .slli rd rs1 shamt else .unknown
93	      | _   => .unknown
94	  | 0x33 => -- OP
95	      if funct7 = 0 then
96	        match funct3 with
97	        | 0x0 => .add rd rs1 rs2
98	        | 0x6 => .or  rd rs1 rs2
99	        | _   => .unknown
100	      else .
… [truncated 3017 chars]
```

I've read the full status and confirmed your recollection. Here's where things stand.

## Current status

The hex0 verification tower is **essentially complete** except for one item:

| Layer | State |
|---|---|
| Bare-metal run (`qemu-system-riscv64`) → `Hello\n` | ✅ runs |
| `decode` spec (Lean + Coq), cross-checked | ✅ |
| Grammar ⟺ spec (HEX0.md BNF ⟺ `decodeS`, total + deterministic) | ✅ proved |
| Finite certification (deployed bytes = `coreSpec`) | ✅ proved (Coq kernel-checked) |
| **General refinement** `core_refines` (∀ inputs, real bytes = `coreSpec`) | ✅ **proved in BOTH** Lean (`sorry`-free) and Coq (`Admitted`-free) |

So the big theorem is done in both assistants. The git log confirms it — the last ~25 commits were closing the Coq `loop_iteration` dispatch, ending at `46089fa docs: Coq core_refines fully PROVED`.

## The one remaining task — and it's tractable here

You're right: **task #7, the ISA cross-check**, is the only open item. It's the #1 entry in the "Trusted (IN the TCB)" list in `TCB.md`:

> The hand-written RV64I model (`Rv64i.{v,lean}` — decode + step for the 12 forms `ADDI ADD OR SLLI LBU SB BEQ BLT BGE BGEU JAL JALR`) is currently justified **empirically** (matches QEMU on the battery). Making it proof-grade means cross-checking decode+step against an authoritative model.

The docs (`RESUME.md` §"Things NOT yet done") were pessimistic about this, noting `sail-riscv-lean` is "171k LoC, WIP, not executable." **But I found something better already installed**: the opam switch has **`coq-riscv` (the MIT `riscv-coq` / riscv-semantics model — the bedrock2/compiler spec)** at `~/.opam/.../user-contrib/riscv/`, with `Spec/Decode.v`, `Spec/ExecuteI.v`, `Spec/Machine.v`. I verified **all 12 of our instruction forms exist in its `InstructionI` inductive** (`Addi Add Or Slli Lbu Sb Beq Blt Bge Bgeu Jal Jalr`). So the Coq side of the cross-check is genuinely doable against a real, kernel-checked oracle — no 171k-line Sail dependency needed.

## Proposed approach for the Coq cross-check

The clean, low-TCB form is a **decode agreement theorem**: for every 32-bit word `w`, our `Rv64i.decode w` and riscv-coq's `Decode.decode RV64I w` produce corresponding instructions (same opcode/regs/immediates), and our `step` matches their `Execute.execute` semantics on those 12 forms. Two sub-parts:

1. **Decode equivalence** — map our `Instr` to their `InstructionI`, prove agreement. Their `Proofs/DecodeEncode.v` gives encode/decode round-trip lemmas we can lean on.
2. **Execute equivalence** — our `step` vs their `execute` instantiated at a concrete `RiscvMachine`/state-monad, for the 12 forms (register read/write, PC, byte load/store, signed/unsigned branch).

Before I start building, one scoping decision is worth your call:

Definition execute {p : Type -> Type} {t : Type} `{Spec.Machine.RiscvMachine p
                                                                             t}
   : Spec.Decode.InstructionI -> p unit :=
  fun arg_0__ =>
    match arg_0__ with
    | Spec.Decode.Lui rd imm20 =>
        Spec.Machine.setRegister rd (Utility.Utility.fromImm imm20)
    | Spec.Decode.Auipc rd oimm20 =>
        Bind Spec.Machine.getPC (fun pc =>
                Spec.Machine.setRegister rd (Utility.Utility.fromImm oimm20 + pc))

        Bind Spec.Machine.getPC (fun pc =>
                let newPC := pc + Utility.Utility.fromImm jimm20 in
                if (Utility.Utility.remu newPC (ZToReg 4) /= ZToReg 0) : bool
                then Spec.Machine.raiseExceptionWithInfo (ZToReg 0) (ZToReg 0) (id newPC)
                else (Bind (Spec.Machine.setRegister rd (pc + ZToReg 4)) (fun _ =>
                              Spec.Machine.setPC newPC)))
    | Spec.Decode.Jalr rd rs1 oimm12 =>
        Bind (Spec.Machine.getRegister rs1) (fun x =>
                Bind Spec.Machine.getPC (fun pc =>
                        let newPC := and (x + Utility.Utility.fromImm oimm12) (lnot (ZToReg 1)) in
                        if (Utility.Utility.remu newPC (ZToReg 4) /= ZToReg 0) : bool
                        then Spec.Machine.raiseExceptionWithInfo (ZToReg 0) (ZToReg 0) (id newPC)
                        else (Bind (Spec.Machine.setRegister rd (pc + ZToReg 4)) (fun _ =>
                                      Spec.Machine.setPC newPC))))

        Bind (Spec.Machine.getRegister rs1) (fun x =>

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  22:03:21; tool 9ms

```
1	(** * A minimal, executable RV64I model in Coq -- mirror of lean/Hex0/Rv64i.lean.
2	
3	    Same 12 instruction encodings used by bare/core.s:
4	      ADDI ADD OR SLLI LBU SB BEQ BLT BGE BGEU JAL JALR
5	    64-bit words are [Z] kept in [0, 2^64); operations wrap explicitly. Memory
6	    is byte-addressed ([Z -> Z], bytes in [0,256)). The model computes under
7	    [vm_compute] so it can be run on the real binary bytes (see Validate.v). *)
8	
9	From Coq Require Import ZArith List Lia Bool.
10	Import ListNotations.
11	Local Open Scope Z_scope.
12	
13	Definition w64 : Z := 2 ^ 64.
14	
15	Definition wrap (z : Z) : Z := z mod w64.
16	Definition wadd (a b : Z) : Z := wrap (a + b).
17	Definition wor  (a b : Z) : Z := Z.lor a b.
18	Definition wshl (a : Z) (n : Z) : Z := wrap (Z.shiftl a n).
19	
20	(* sign-extend a [k]-bit raw value to a (possibly negative) Z *)
21	Definition sext (k raw : Z) : Z :=
22	  if raw >=? 2 ^ (k - 1) then raw - 2 ^ k else raw.
23	
24	(* unsigned / signed comparisons on in-range words *)
25	Definition toS (x : Z) : Z := if x >=? 2 ^ 63 then x - w64 else x.
26	Definition ultb (a b : Z) : bool := a <? b.
27	Definition sltb (a b : Z) : bool := toS a <? toS b.
28	
29	(* extract [len] bits at offset [lo] from a 32-bit value *)
30	Definition field (w lo len : Z) : Z := (w / 2 ^ lo) mod 2 ^ len.
31	
32	Record State := mkState {
33	  reg : Z -> Z;     (* x0..x31 ; x0 forced to 0 by rget/rset *)
34	  pc  : Z;
35	  mem : Z -> Z      (* byte-addressed *)
36	}.
37	
38	Definition rget (s : State) (i : Z) : Z := if i =? 0 then 0 else s.(reg) i.
39	
40	Definition rset (s : State) (i : Z) (v : Z) : State :=
41	  if i =? 0 then s
42	  else mkState (fun j => if j =? i then v else s.(reg) j) s.(pc) s.(mem).
43	
44	Definition setPc (s : State) (p : Z) : State := mkState s.(reg) p s.(mem).
45	
46	Definition storeByte (s : State) (a b : Z) : State :=
47	  mkState s.(reg) s.(pc) (fun x => if x =? a then b mod 256 else s.(mem) x).
48	
49	Definition fetch32 (s : State) : Z :=
50	  let b0 := s.(mem) s.(pc) in
51	  let b1 := s.(mem) (s.(pc) + 1) in
52	  let b2 := s.(mem) (s.(pc) + 2) in
53	  let b3 := s.(mem) (s.(pc) + 3) in
54	  b0 + b1 * 256 + b2 * 65536 + b3 * 16777216.
55	
56	Inductive Instr :=
57	  | Iaddi (rd rs1 : Z) (imm : Z)
58	  | Iadd  (rd rs1 rs2 : Z)
59	  | Ior   (rd rs1 rs2 : Z)
60	  | Islli (rd rs1 : Z) (shamt : Z)
61	  | Ilbu  (rd rs1 : Z) (imm : Z)
62	  | Isb   (rs1 rs2 : Z) (imm : Z)
63	  | Ibeq  (rs1 rs2 : Z) (imm : Z)
64	  | Iblt  (rs1 rs2 : Z) (imm : Z)
65	  | Ibge  (rs1 rs2 : Z) (imm : Z)
66	  | Ibgeu (rs1 rs2 : Z) (imm : Z)
67	  | Ijal  (rd : Z) (imm : Z)
68	  | Ijalr (rd rs1 : Z) (imm : Z)
69	  | Iunknown.
70	
71	(* immediates are stored as sign-extended Z, ready to feed into wadd *)
72	Definition decode (w : Z) : Instr :=
73	  let opcode := field w 0 7 in
74	  let rd     := field w 7 5 in
75	  let funct3 := field w 12 3 in
76	  let rs1    := field w 15 5 in
77	  let rs2    := field w 20 5 in
78	  let funct7 := field w 25 7 in
79	  let immI   := sext 12 (field w 20 12) in
80	  let shamt  := field w 20 6 in
81	  let immS   := sext 12 (Z.lor (Z.shiftl funct7 5) rd) in
82	  let immB   := sext 13 (Z.lor (Z.lor (Z.shiftl (field w 31 1) 12) (Z.shiftl (field w 7 1) 11))
83	                               (Z.lor (Z.shiftl (field w 25 6) 5) (Z.shiftl (field w 8 4) 1))) in
84	  let immJ   := sext 21 (Z.lor (Z.lor (Z.shiftl (field w 31 1) 20) (Z.shiftl (field w 12 8) 12))
85	                               (Z.lor (Z.shiftl (field w 20 1) 11) (Z.shiftl (field w 21 10) 1))) in
86	  if opcode =? 19 then            (* 0x13 OP-IMM *)
87	    if funct3 =? 0 then Iaddi rd rs1 immI
88	    else if funct3 =? 1 then (if funct7 =? 0 then Islli rd rs1 shamt else Iunknown)
89	    else Iunknown
90	  else if opcode =? 51 then       (* 0x33 OP *)
91	    if funct7 =? 0 then
92	      (if funct3 =? 0 then Iadd rd rs1 rs2
93	       else if funct3 =? 6 then Ior rd rs1 rs2 else Iunknown)
94	    else Iunknown
95	  else if opcode =? 3 then        (* 
… [truncated 2321 chars]

Require Import Decode.
Require ExecuteI.
Require ExecuteI64.
Require ExecuteM.
Require ExecuteM64.
Require ExecuteCSR.
Require Import Monads.
Require Import riscv.Spec.Machine.
Require Import Utility.

(* Note: Filtering of unsupported instructions was already done in Decode, and they are
   turned into `InvalidInstruction i` *)
Definition execute {p} {t} `{(RiscvMachine p t)}(inst: Instruction): p unit :=
  match inst with
  | IInstruction i       => ExecuteI.execute i
  | MInstruction i       => ExecuteM.execute i
  | I64Instruction i     => ExecuteI64.execute i
  | M64Instruction i     => ExecuteM64.execute i
  | CSRInstruction i     => ExecuteCSR.execute i
  | InvalidInstruction i => raiseExceptionWithInfo (ZToReg 0) (ZToReg 2) (ZToReg i)
  (* Not supported by this spec: *)
  | AInstruction _ | FInstruction _ | A64Instruction _ | F64Instruction _ => raiseException (ZToReg 0) (ZToReg 2)
  end.

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  22:04:22; tool 61ms

```
########## run1 body ##########
Section Riscv.

  Context {mword: Type}.
  Context {MW: MachineWidth mword}.

  Context {M: Type -> Type}.
  Context {MM: Monad M}.
  Context {RVP: RiscvProgram M mword}.
  Context {RVS: RiscvMachine M mword}.

  Definition run1(iset: InstructionSet):
    M unit :=
    pc <- getPC;
    inst <- loadWord Fetch pc;
    execute (decode iset (combine 4 inst));;
    endCycleNormal.

  (* Note: We cannot use
     power_func (fun m => run1 iset;; m) n (Return tt)
     to obtain a monadic computation executing n instructions,
########## Minimal: getPC/setPC/loadByte/storeByte/translate/getRegister ##########
    match o with
    | Some x => Return x
    | None => fail_hard
    end.

  Definition loadN(n: nat)(kind: SourceType)(a: word): OState RiscvMachine (HList.tuple byte n) :=
    mach <- get;
    v <- fail_if_None (Memory.load_bytes n mach.(getMem) a);
    match kind with
    | Fetch => if isXAddr4B a mach.(getXAddrs) then Return v else fail_hard
    | _ => Return v
    end.

  Definition storeN(n: nat)(kind: SourceType)(a: word)(v: HList.tuple byte n) :=
    mach <- get;
    m <- fail_if_None (Memory.store_bytes n mach.(getMem) a v);
    update (fun mach =>
              withXAddrs (invalidateWrittenXAddrs n a mach.(getXAddrs)) (withMem m mach)).

  Instance IsRiscvMachine: RiscvProgram (OState RiscvMachine) word :=  {
      getRegister reg :=
        if Z.eq_dec reg Register0 then
          Return (ZToReg 0)
        else
          if (0 <? reg) && (reg <? 32) then
            mach <- get;
            match map.get mach.(getRegs) reg with
            | Some v => Return v
            | None => Return (word.of_Z 0)
            end
          else
            fail_hard;

      setRegister reg v :=
        if Z.eq_dec reg Register0 then
          Return tt
        else
          if (0 <? reg) && (reg <? 32) then
            update (fun mach => withRegs (map.put mach.(getRegs) reg v) mach)
          else
            fail_hard;

      getPC := mach <- get; Return mach.(getPc);

      setPC newPC := update (withNextPc newPC);

      loadByte   := loadN 1;
      loadHalf   := loadN 2;
      loadWord   := loadN 4;
      loadDouble := loadN 8;

      storeByte   := storeN 1;
      storeHalf   := storeN 2;
      storeWord   := storeN 4;
      storeDouble := storeN 8;

      makeReservation  addr := fail_hard;
      clearReservation addr := fail_hard;
      checkReservation addr := fail_hard;
      getCSRField f := fail_hard;
      setCSRField f v := fail_hard;
      getPrivMode := fail_hard;
      setPrivMode v := fail_hard;
      fence _ _ := fail_hard;

      endCycleNormal := update (fun m => (withPc m.(getNextPc)
                                         (withNextPc (word.add m.(getNextPc) (word.of_Z 4)) m)));

      (* fail hard if exception is thrown because at the moment, we want to prove that
         code output by the compiler never throws exceptions *)
      endCycleEarly{A: Type} := fail_hard;
```

Done — recon complete and the plan is written to `CROSSCHECK.md`. Here's what I found.

## Confirmation

You're right: **task #7 (ISA cross-check) is the sole open item.** Everything above the ISA layer — `core_refines`, the grammar equivalence, the certifications — is fully proved in both Lean and Coq. The one thing still *trusted* (not proved) is `TCB.md` item 1: "our hand-rolled RV64I model is faithful to real RISC-V," currently justified only empirically (matches QEMU on a battery).

## The key discovery (changes the outlook)

`RESUME.md` was pessimistic — it assumed the only oracle was `sail-riscv-lean` (171k LoC, WIP, "not executable"). But the opam switch **already has `coq-riscv.0.0.5` installed** — the MIT **riscv-coq** model (the bedrock2/`compiler` semantics, generated from the official Haskell `riscv-semantics`), plus `coqutil`. It loads cleanly (`Require Import riscv.Spec.Decode.` just works), all 12 of our instruction forms exist in its `InstructionI`, and it reduces under `vm_compute`. This is a far better target than Sail.

## Strongest evidence: it already holds empirically

I ran a decode differential over the **real `core` image** — all 81 instruction words, both decoders, field-by-field:

```
allAgree 81   = true     (every core word decodes identically, ours vs riscv-coq)
cntUnknown 81 = 0        (our model decodes every core word to one of the 12 known forms)
```

So on the deployed bytes, our decoder = riscv-coq's decoder, exactly. The proof work is turning that into general theorems.

## The plan (`CROSSCHECK.md`)

Two theorems land in a new `coq/RvCross.v`:
- **T1 `decode_agrees`** — pure, all 32-bit words, self-contained (no monad). ~150–250 lines. **Do first.**
- **T2 `step_agrees`** — our `step` vs riscv-coq's `Run.run1 RV64I` under a `State ↔ RiscvMachine` bridge, over the 12 forms. ~300–500 lines; new machinery is the `coqutil` word/map bridge.

The doc has the full riscv-coq API surface, the state-bridge relation, a 12-row per-instruction mapping table, the lemma DAG, and build integration. It also pins down the **differences the cross-check surfaces** (the actual payoff), e.g.:
- **SLLI `shamt≥32`**: we return `Iunknown`, riscv-coq accepts it (RV64 6-bit shamt) — an intentional, sound narrowing; every `core` SLLI is `shamt=4`.
- **Misaligned branch targets**: riscv-coq raises an exception, we just jump — they agree precisely when targets are 4-aligned (true for `core`), now made an explicit precondition rather than a silent assumption.

Net TCB effect: trade "trust our 136-line bespoke model" for "trust the community reference model" — the standard, much stronger position.

Want me to proceed with **T1 (`decode_agrees`)** — the self-contained decode-agreement proof — as the first implementation step?

### 👤 **User**  ·  22:10:35; waited 1m23s

would it be possible to use the "community reference model" instead of hand-rolled riscv model?

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  22:11:25; model 1m08s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Good question — and it gets at the real goal. Short answer: **yes, but in two quite different senses, and only one of them is a good idea.** Let me separate them.

## Sense (a): rip out the hand-rolled model, rebuild `core_refines` on riscv-coq

Possible *on the Coq side only*, but it's a large step backward in effort and structure:

- **The substrate is much less proof-friendly.** riscv-coq's machine runs in a **partial, monadic** form — `OState RiscvMachine` (`state → option A × state`, with `fail_hard`). Our entire `Refine.v` is built on a **pure, total** `step : State → State` with `runFuel`. Rebuilding means re-deriving all ~56 step/loop lemmas and the whole `loop_iteration`/`loop_correct` induction (the ~2500-line dispatch tail that took the bulk of this project) over monadic binds that thread an `option`. That's redoing the hardest, *already-finished* part on worse footing.
- **State is finite-map-based, not total functions.** Our `mem : Z → Z` / `reg : Z → Z` are total — frame reasoning is just function update, no domain obligations. riscv-coq uses `coqutil` `map.map`, so every access carries a domain side-condition and uses map lemmas. The 16-field `LoopInv` and all the disjointness/frame geometry would get heavier.
- **Words vs Z**, and the `vm_compute`-based **kernel-checked certification** (`Certify.v`) would both need re-validation against coqutil's `word`/maps.
- **There is no Lean equivalent.** `sail-riscv-lean` is 171k LoC, WIP, not executable. So you cannot do this on the Lean side at all — you'd end up with Coq-on-riscv-coq and Lean-on-hand-rolled, **breaking the parallel-mirror structure** that is currently a real strength (two independent assistants checking the same tower).

So sense (a): feasible in Coq, not worth it, and it desyncs the two ports.

## Sense (b): make the *final theorem* be about riscv-coq, keeping the hand-rolled model as an internal proof device

This is the good version, and it's almost free given the plan. The trick is to frame **T2 as a forward simulation** rather than just a per-instruction sanity check:

```
R s m  ∧  WF s m  →  ∃ m', Run.run1 RV64I m = (Some tt, m')  ∧  R (step s) m'
```

If `R` is a simulation relation preserved by each step, then by induction the **whole run** corresponds, and because `observe`/`coreSpec` only read R-related projections (`a0`, `a1`, output region), the already-proven `core_refines` **transports** along `R` to give:

```
core_refines_riscv : ∀ inp cap, WellFormed inp cap →
    ∃ n, observe_riscv (run1^n (init_riscv inp cap)) = coreSpec inp cap
```

i.e. *"the community reference model, running the real bytes, implements the hex0 spec"* — obtained by **composing the existing (done) refinement with the simulation**, with **no rewrite of `Refine.v`**. The hand-rolled model is then demoted from "a thing you trust" to "a convenient intermediate the proof factors through," and the *headline result* is stated over riscv-coq.

So sense (b) delivers exactly what your question is really after — getting the reference model into the trusted result — without paying the sense-(a) cost, and it keeps the Lean mirror intact (Lean keeps its hand-rolled model as the proof device; the Coq side carries the riscv-coq transport).

## Recommendation

Do the cross-check, but **frame T2 as a simulation and add the transport corollary** `core_refines_riscv`. That makes the final Coq theorem speak about the community model directly — effectively "using" riscv-coq as the semantics — while reusing the finished `core_refines` instead of rebuilding it.

The one caveat to verify during implementation: the transport needs `R` to be a *functional/deterministic* simulation (Minimal's `OState` is deterministic, so this holds) and that `init_riscv inp cap` is R-related to our `mkInit` (a prologue lemma analogous to the existing `init_loopinv`).

Want me to fold this "simulation + transport" framing into `CROSSCHECK.md` (it sharpens T2 and adds the `core_refines_riscv` corollary as the real deliverable), and then start on T1?

Definition bitSlice(x: Z)(start eend: Z): Z :=
  Z.land (Z.shiftr x start) (Z.lnot (Z.shiftl (-1) (eend - start))).
Definition bitSlice'(w start eend: Z): Z :=
  (w / 2 ^ start) mod (2 ^ (eend - start)).
---signExtend---
Definition signExtend(oldwidth: Z)(z: Z): Z :=
  (z + 2^(oldwidth-1)) mod 2^oldwidth - 2^(oldwidth-1).
Definition signExtend_bitwise(width n: Z): Z :=
  if Z.testbit n (width - 1)
  then (Z.lor (Z.land n (Z.ones width)) (Z.shiftl (-1) width))
  else (Z.land n (Z.ones width)).

I now fully understand riscv-coq's `decode`: for `RV64I` (`supportsM=false`, `bitwidth=64`), the result list collapses so that whenever `decodeI` is a valid I-instruction (and no I64/CSR also matches), `decode RV64I w = IInstruction decodeI`. The bridges I need are `field ↔ bitSlice` and `sext ↔ signExtend`. Notably, the SLLI `shamt≥32` gap does **not** affect T1 (it only bites the reverse direction), so T1 is clean.

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  22:15:50; tool 72ms

```
Definition bitSlice(x: Z)(start eend: Z): Z :=
  Z.land (Z.shiftr x start) (Z.lnot (Z.shiftl (-1) (eend - start))).

Definition bitSlice'(w start eend: Z): Z :=
  (w / 2 ^ start) mod (2 ^ (eend - start)).

Lemma bitSlice_alt: forall w start eend,
    0 <= start <= eend ->
    bitSlice w start eend = bitSlice' w start eend.
Proof.
  intros. unfold bitSlice, bitSlice'.
  rewrite <- Z.land_ones by blia.
  rewrite <- Z.shiftr_div_pow2 by blia.
  f_equal.
  rewrite Z.shiftl_mul_pow2 by blia.
  rewrite Z.mul_comm.
  rewrite <- Z.opp_eq_mul_m1.
  replace (Z.lnot (- 2 ^ (eend - start))) with (2 ^ (eend - start) - 1).
  - rewrite Z.ones_equiv. reflexivity.
  - pose proof (Z.add_lnot_diag (- 2 ^ (eend - start))). blia.
Qed.

Lemma bitSlice_range: forall sz z,
    0 <= sz ->
```

My plan is to make `bitSlice`/`signExtend` opaque (so operands stay abstract), rewrite only the control fields (opcode/funct3) to concrete values, then `cbn` the boolean guards and list-combination. ```
=== prove_Zeq_bitwise.v (interface) ===
(* same application area as "bitblast", but a bit more complex and a bit more powerful *)

Require Import Coq.ZArith.ZArith.
Require Import coqutil.Z.Lia.
Require Import coqutil.Z.BitOps.
Require Export Coq.setoid_ring.ZArithRing.
Require Import Coq.btauto.Btauto.

Local Open Scope bool_scope.
Local Open Scope Z_scope.


Tactic Notation "safe_ring_simplify" constr(i) "in" ident(C) :=
  first [ring_simplify i in C |
         let t := type of i in fail 1000 "No ring structure found for" t ].

Lemma testbit_minus1: forall i,
    0 <= i ->
    Z.testbit (-1) i = true.
Proof.
  intros. rewrite (Z.bits_opp 1) by assumption.
  simpl. rewrite Z.bits_0. reflexivity.
Qed.

Lemma testbit_above: forall {p n},
    0 <= n < 2 ^ p ->
    0 <= p ->
    forall i,
    p <= i ->
    Z.testbit n i = false.
Proof.
  intros.
  rewrite <- (Z.mod_small n (2 ^ p)) by assumption.
  apply Z.mod_pow2_bits_high.
  auto.
Qed.

Lemma if_same: forall (A: Type) (b: bool) (a: A),
    (if b then a else a) = a.
Proof.
  intros. destruct b; reflexivity.
Qed.

Lemma then_true_else_false: forall (b: bool),
    (if b then true else false) = b.
Proof.
  intros. destruct b; reflexivity.
Qed.

#[global] Hint Rewrite
     if_same
     then_true_else_false
     Bool.andb_false_r
     Bool.andb_true_r
     Bool.andb_false_l
     Bool.andb_true_l
     Bool.orb_false_r
     Bool.orb_true_r
     Bool.orb_false_l
     Bool.orb_true_l
=== how riscv DecodeEncode uses it ===

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  22:23:47; tool 561ms

```
Lemma bitSlice_range: forall sz z,
    0 <= sz ->
    0 <= bitSlice z 0 sz < 2 ^ sz.
Proof.
  intros.
  rewrite bitSlice_alt by blia.
  unfold bitSlice'.
  change (2 ^ 0) with 1.
  rewrite Z.div_1_r.
  rewrite Z.sub_0_r.
  apply Z.mod_pos_bound.
  apply Z.pow_pos_nonneg; blia.
Qed.

Lemma signExtend_range: forall i z,
    0 < i ->
    - 2 ^ (i - 1) <= signExtend i z < 2 ^ (i - 1).
Proof.
  intros.
  unfold signExtend.
  pose proof (Z.mod_pos_bound (z + (2 ^ (i - 1))) (2 ^ i)) as P.
  assert (0 < 2 ^ i) as A. {
    apply Z.pow_pos_nonneg; blia.
  }
  specialize (P A).
  replace (2 ^ i) with (2 ^ ((i - 1) + 1)) in * by (f_equal; blia).
  rewrite Z.pow_add_r in * by blia.
  change (2 ^ 1) with 2 in *.
  remember (2 ^ (i - 1)) as B.
  blia.
Qed.

Lemma signExtend_bounds: forall i z,
    0 <= i -> - 2 ^ i <= signExtend (i + 1) z < 2 ^ i.
Proof.
  intros. pose proof (signExtend_range (i + 1) z) as P.
  replace (i + 1 - 1) with i in P by Lia.lia. eapply P. Lia.lia.
Qed.

Lemma signExtend_nop: forall l w v,
    - 2 ^ l <= v < 2 ^ l ->
    0 <= l < w ->
```

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  22:37:12; tool 94ms

```
############ RiscvMachine record + withX setters + Mem/load_bytes ############

Section Machine.

  Context {width: Z} {word: word width} {word_ok: word.ok word}.
  Context {Registers: map.map Register word}.
  Context {Mem: map.map word byte}.

  (* (memory before call, call name, arg values) and (memory after call, return values) *)
  Definition LogItem{_: Bitwidth width}: Type := (Mem * string * list word) * (Mem * list word).

  (* set of executable addresses. On some processors, this could be the whole address range,
     while on others, only a specific range. And when an address is written, we might
     conservatively remove it from that set if we want to prove that our software does not
     depend on self-modifying code being possible.
     The ifence instruction will flush the instruction cache and therefore put back the
     set of executable addresses to the whole range. *)
  Definition XAddrs: Type := list word.

  Definition isXAddr1B(a: word)(xAddrs: XAddrs): bool :=
    match List.find (word.eqb a) xAddrs with
    | Some _ => true
    | None => false
    end.

  Definition isXAddr4B(a: word)(xAddrs: XAddrs): bool :=
    isXAddr1B a xAddrs &&
    isXAddr1B (word.add a (word.of_Z 1)) xAddrs &&
    isXAddr1B (word.add a (word.of_Z 2)) xAddrs &&
    isXAddr1B (word.add a (word.of_Z 3)) xAddrs.

  Definition isXAddr1: word -> XAddrs -> Prop := @List.In word.

  Definition isXAddr4(a: word)(xAddrs: XAddrs): Prop :=
    isXAddr1 a xAddrs /\
    isXAddr1 (word.add a (word.of_Z 1)) xAddrs /\
    isXAddr1 (word.add a (word.of_Z 2)) xAddrs /\
    isXAddr1 (word.add a (word.of_Z 3)) xAddrs.

  Lemma isXAddr1B_holds: forall a xAddrs,
      isXAddr1B a xAddrs = true -> isXAddr1 a xAddrs.
  Proof.
    unfold isXAddr1B, isXAddr1. intros.
    destruct (List.find (word.eqb a) xAddrs) eqn: E; [|discriminate].
    apply List.find_some in E. destruct E.
    apply Word.Properties.word.eqb_true in H1.
    subst. assumption.
  Qed.

  Lemma isXAddr1B_not: forall a xAddrs,
      isXAddr1B a xAddrs = false -> ~ isXAddr1 a xAddrs.
  Proof.
############ Memory.load_bytes / store_bytes ############
21:  Definition footprint(a: word)(sz: nat): tuple word sz :=
24:  Definition load_bytes(sz: nat)(m: mem)(addr: word): option (tuple byte sz) :=
25:    map.getmany_of_tuple m (footprint addr sz).
27:  Definition unchecked_store_bytes(sz: nat)(m: mem)(a: word)(bs: tuple byte sz): mem :=
28:    map.putmany_of_tuple (footprint a sz) bs m.
30:  Definition store_bytes(sz: nat)(m: mem)(a: word)(v: tuple byte sz): option mem :=
36:  Definition unchecked_store_byte_list(a: word)(l: list byte)(m: mem): mem :=
66:    - destruct (map.getmany_of_tuple m (footprint a (S n))) eqn: E; [|discriminate].
```

```coq
Theorem decode_agrees : forall w, 0 <= w < 2^32 ->
  forall i, Rv64i.decode w = i -> i <> Iunknown -> Decode.decode RV64I w = embed i.
```

## ◻ T2 — execute/step cross-check: designed + instantiation verified

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  22:45:18; tool 102ms

```
############ Minimal.v full instance (40-110) ############
    | _ => Return v
    end.

  Definition storeN(n: nat)(kind: SourceType)(a: word)(v: HList.tuple byte n) :=
    mach <- get;
    m <- fail_if_None (Memory.store_bytes n mach.(getMem) a v);
    update (fun mach =>
              withXAddrs (invalidateWrittenXAddrs n a mach.(getXAddrs)) (withMem m mach)).

  Instance IsRiscvMachine: RiscvProgram (OState RiscvMachine) word :=  {
      getRegister reg :=
        if Z.eq_dec reg Register0 then
          Return (ZToReg 0)
        else
          if (0 <? reg) && (reg <? 32) then
            mach <- get;
            match map.get mach.(getRegs) reg with
            | Some v => Return v
            | None => Return (word.of_Z 0)
            end
          else
            fail_hard;

      setRegister reg v :=
        if Z.eq_dec reg Register0 then
          Return tt
        else
          if (0 <? reg) && (reg <? 32) then
            update (fun mach => withRegs (map.put mach.(getRegs) reg v) mach)
          else
            fail_hard;

      getPC := mach <- get; Return mach.(getPc);

      setPC newPC := update (withNextPc newPC);

      loadByte   := loadN 1;
      loadHalf   := loadN 2;
      loadWord   := loadN 4;
      loadDouble := loadN 8;

      storeByte   := storeN 1;
      storeHalf   := storeN 2;
      storeWord   := storeN 4;
      storeDouble := storeN 8;

      makeReservation  addr := fail_hard;
      clearReservation addr := fail_hard;
      checkReservation addr := fail_hard;
      getCSRField f := fail_hard;
      setCSRField f v := fail_hard;
      getPrivMode := fail_hard;
      setPrivMode v := fail_hard;
      fence _ _ := fail_hard;

      endCycleNormal := update (fun m => (withPc m.(getNextPc)
                                         (withNextPc (word.add m.(getNextPc) (word.of_Z 4)) m)));

      (* fail hard if exception is thrown because at the moment, we want to prove that
         code output by the compiler never throws exceptions *)
      endCycleEarly{A: Type} := fail_hard;
  }.

  Arguments Memory.load_bytes: simpl never.
  Arguments Memory.store_bytes: simpl never.

  Lemma VirtualMemoryFetchP: forall (addr: word) xAddrs,
      VirtualMemory = Fetch -> isXAddr4 addr xAddrs.
  Proof. intros. discriminate. Qed.

  Lemma ExecuteFetchP: forall (addr: word) xAddrs,
############ OState Bind/get/put exact defs ############
Definition OState(S A: Type) := S -> (option A) * S.

#[global] Instance OState_Monad(S: Type): Monad (OState S). refine ({|
  Bind A B (m: OState S A) (f: A -> OState S B) :=
    fun (s: S) => match m s with
                  | (Some a, s') => f a s'
                  | (None, s') => (None, s')
                  end;
  Return A (a: A) := fun (s: S) => (Some a, s)
|}).
all: prove_monad_law.
Defined.

Module OStateOperations.

  Definition get{S: Type}: OState S S := fun (s: S) => (Some s, s).

  Definition put{S: Type}(s: S): OState S unit := fun _ => (Some tt, s).

  Definition fail_hard{S A: Type}: OState S A :=
    fun (s: S) => (None, s).

  #[global] Hint Unfold get put fail_hard : unf_monad_ops.

  Lemma Bind_get{S A: Type}: forall (f: S -> OState S A) (s: S),
      Bind get f s = f s s.
  Proof. prove_monad_law. Qed.

  Lemma Bind_put{S A: Type}: forall (f: unit -> OState S A) (s0 s1: S),
      Bind (put s1) f s0 = f tt s1.
  Proof. prove_monad_law. Qed.

  (* provides the link between "S -> option A * S" and "S -> (S -> Prop) -> Prop" *)
  Definition computation_satisfies{S: Type}(m: OState S unit)(s: S)(post: S -> Prop): Prop :=
    exists s', m s = (Some tt, s') /\ post s'.
```

=== footprint + tuple.unfoldn ===
Section MemAccess.
  Context {width} {word: word width} {mem: map.map word byte}.

  Definition footprint(a: word)(sz: nat): tuple word sz :=
    tuple.unfoldn (fun w => word.add w (word.of_Z 1)) sz a.

  Definition load_bytes(sz: nat)(m: mem)(addr: word): option (tuple byte sz) :=
    map.getmany_of_tuple m (footprint addr sz).

  Definition unchecked_store_bytes(sz: nat)(m: mem)(a: word)(bs: tuple byte sz): mem :=
    map.putmany_of_tuple (footprint a sz) bs m.

  Definition store_bytes(sz: nat)(m: mem)(a: word)(v: tuple byte sz): option mem :=
    match load_bytes sz m a with
    | Some _ => Some (unchecked_store_bytes sz m a v)

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  22:53:25; tool 88ms

```
Lemma or_to_plus: forall a b,
    Z.land a b = 0 ->
    Z.lor a b = a + b.
Proof.
  intros.
  rewrite <- Z.lxor_lor by assumption.
  symmetry. apply Z.add_nocarry_lxor. assumption.
Qed.


(** ** bitSlice *)
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  23:04:39; model 24.1s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Two T2 installments are committed. Here's the progress.

## T2 — execute/step cross-check: foundation landed

Branch `isa-crosscheck-decode`, commit `fb4f58d` (after the T1 commit `63840f4`):

**`coq/RvCrossStep.v`** — the two instruction-independent foundations of the forward simulation, **all `Admitted`-free, in the `make` build**:

1. **Word/Z arithmetic bridge** — `br_add`, `br_or`, `br_ltu`, `br_lts` (+ `toS_signed`, `wrap64`): every riscv-coq `word 64` operation `ExecuteI` uses computes our corresponding `Z`-mod-2⁶⁴ op (`wadd`/`wor`/`ultb`/`sltb`) under `word.unsigned`. The signed-compare bridge (`br_lts` via `toS_signed`) was the subtle one — done.

2. **Fetch bridge** `fetch_combine` (the keystone) — one `run1` instruction fetch (the `LittleEndian.combine` of the 4 bytes `load_bytes 4` reads from the riscv map) equals the 32-bit word our `fetch32` reads. This was the hardest shared lemma: footprint address arithmetic via bedrock2 `ZnWords`, byte-disjointness via `land_lo_hi`/`or_to_plus`, `le_combine` reduced through `combine_eq`.

3. **State-bridge relation** `Rrel = RegAgree ∧ MemAgree D ∧ PcAgree` + fetch well-formedness `WFfetch`, type-checked against the concrete Minimal `RiscvMachine` record.

## Where T2 stands

| Piece | State |
|---|---|
| Concrete machine instantiation | ✅ verified type-checks |
| Word/Z arithmetic bridge | ✅ proved |
| Fetch bridge (`combine 4 = fetch32`) | ✅ proved (keystone) |
| State-bridge relation `Rrel`/`WFfetch` | ✅ defined |
| `run1` `OState` monad reduction | ◻ next |
| 12 `exec_*` lemmas (incl. `sb` store, branches) | ◻ |
| `step_agrees` assembly + `core_refines_riscv` transport | ◻ |

The remaining work is the `run1` monad reduction (`Bind`/`get`/`put` are plain functions, so it reduces) feeding into the per-instruction `exec_*` lemmas — the register/memory bridges + `decode_agrees` (T1) slot in here — then assembly and transport.

This was a natural commit boundary (the foundation is a self-contained, reusable unit). The next chunk is the `run1` reduction + the first end-to-end `exec_addi`, which validates the per-instruction pattern. I can continue straight into that — want me to keep going, or is this a good point to pause and review the two committed installments?

## T2 status — all reusable infrastructure is proven

The hard, shared machinery of the execute/step simulation is now done:

- **Arithmetic**: every `word 64` op `ExecuteI` uses = our `Z`-mod-2⁶⁴ op (`br_add/or/ltu/lts`), and `wadd_of_Z` for the post-state register value.
- **Fetch**: `fetch_combine` — one `run1` fetch = our `fetch32` (the keystone).
- **Monad reduction**: `run1_fetch` collapses a Minimal `OState` cycle to `execute (decode …)` + `endCycleNormal`; `getReg_red`/`setReg_red`/`endcycle_red`/`getReg_R` reduce the register/PC operations.
- **State bridge**: `Rrel = RegAgree ∧ MemAgree D ∧ PcAgree` defined and type-checked against the concrete machine.

I verified the per-instruction recipe end-to-end in scratch (`run1_fetch → combine=fetch32 → decode_agrees → execute reduction → reassemble Rrel`) — every prerequisite compiles. What remains is mechanical assembly: the 12 `exec_*` lemmas (incl. the x0/rd casing, the `sb` store via `putmany`, and branch targets), `step_agrees` combining them, and the `core_refines_riscv` transport corollary. CROSSCHECK.md and STATUS.md (row 7b) track this.
